## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reaction rate laws / ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A in a chemical reaction, indicating an ordinary differential equation rate law. With only (t, A) available, the most likely structures are concentration-dependent rate laws (reaction order, reversible/approach-to-equilibrium terms) and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing or time-varying rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (A depleted at constant rate; reagent in excess or surface-limited)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed/source term in a batch balance)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; elementary first-order step)
- First-order with source/sink (CSTR/batch with feed): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production plus first-order removal/decay)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or 2A -> products)
- General n-th order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular + bimolecular loss)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (linear return toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible with forward/backward-like terms: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (net rate from opposing linear processes; approach to steady state)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/carrying capacity; autocatalysis + limitation)
- Inhibited/limited-rate consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to site limitation or inhibition proxy)
- Non-autonomous first-order (time-varying rate): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes exponentially in time, e.g., external program/aging)
- Periodic forcing or modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (externally driven production/consumption; reactor cycling)
- Empirical stretched-exponential modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t**c2) * A (time-dependent deactivation/activation with nonlinearity in t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is always negative and proportional to A, the underlying dynamics are exponential in time (first-order kinetics).
- A constant offset term in dA_dt (e.g., +c0) indicates an external source/feed or baseline generation independent of A.
- Higher reaction order (A**c1 with c1>1) typically yields faster initial decay at high A and strong curvature when plotting dA_dt vs A.
- A linear relaxation term c0*(c1-A) implies approach to a finite steady-state concentration c1 (equilibrium/steady-state behavior).
- Competing mechanisms often appear as sums of terms with different powers of A (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2), identifiable by nonlinearity in dA_dt vs A.
- Autocatalysis/limited-growth forms (A*(c1-A)) imply sigmoidal time courses for A and a peak in dA_dt at intermediate A.
- Rational forms like A/(A+c1) indicate rate-limiting saturation (site limitation) where increasing A eventually stops increasing the magnitude of dA_dt.
- Explicit dependence on t (e.g., exp(c*t), sin(c*t)) suggests non-autonomous kinetics due to changing conditions (light intensity, catalyst deactivation, programmed feeds).

### 1. `c0*exp(A*c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*Abs(A*c5) + 1) + c6) + c7*log(A*c8 + 1)`

- **No match.**

### 2. `A*c0 + c1*sin(c2 + c3*log(c4*Abs(A) + 1))`

  - `c1 = 0.49113636468363491`
- **Match found (with domain \(A\ge 0\)).**

### 3. `A*c0 + c1*sin(c2*log(c3*Abs(A*c4) + 1) + c5)`

### 5. `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*Abs(A) + 1) + c5)`

### 6. `A*c0/(A + c1) + c2*sqrt(A**2) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(...))`
- Contains rational term `A*c0/(A+c1)` (not linear globally), `sqrt(A^2)=|A|`, constant, and an exponential-of-sine term.
- You can zero some parts (`c4=0`, `c3=0`, `c0=0`), but then you only get `c2*|A|`, which canŌĆÖt produce both linear and sine(log).

- **No match.**
